Topic: Logic
Context: The basis of life-the main component of protein is an amino acid molecule.It is an organic molecule.Although people have not directly observed amino acid molecules in cosmic space, scientists have used hydrogen, water, oxygen, methane and formaldehyde in the laboratory to simulate the natural conditions of space.Kinds of amino acids.The raw materials used to synthesize amino acids are abundant in interstellar molecules.It is not difficult to imagine that there must also be amino acid molecules in the universe.As long as there is an appropriate environment, they may be transformed into proteins and further develop into organic life.According to this speculation, there are living bodies on other planets than the earth, and may even be living bodies with higher intelligence.
Question: Which of the following is true to best refute the above speculation?
Choices:
  A: There is a huge difference between the process of developing from protein to organic life and the process from organic molecules to protein
  B: Higher intelligence is not only a product of material evolution, but also a product of continuous socialization
  C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event
  D: Some interstellar molecules are not found in the Earth â€™s environment, and they are still not available in the laboratory
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The speculation is that there might be living bodies on other planets than the earth.
  The reasoning is that amino acid molecules can be synthesized from interstellar molecules, which are abundant in the universe.
  To refute this speculation, we need to provide a reason why amino acid molecules cannot be synthesized or why the existence of amino acid molecules does not necessarily result in the development of organic life.
  Choice A provides a reason why the development of organic life cannot be easily achieved even with the presence of amino acid molecules.
  Choice B talks about the factors that contribute to the development of higher intelligence, which is not directly relevant to the speculation.
  Choice C contradicts the speculation by suggesting that the synthesis of amino acid molecules is a rare event.
  Choice D is not relevant to the speculation.
  Therefore, the answer is C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event.

Choices:

  C: Some patients do not believe that the treatment will be effective.Although they have been treated normally, their condition has worsened.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are 6 scholars F, G, J, L, M, and N, who will speak at a logical meeting, and the speeches are arranged in the following order? (1) Each speaker speaks only once, and only once at the same time By.(2) Three speakers speak before lunch, and the other three speak after lunch.(3) G must speak before lunch.(4) Only one speaker is between M and N.(5) F speaks in the first or third place.
Question: If the speeches of M and N are separated by lunch, which of the following lists all speakers that can be arranged between M and N?
Choices:
  A: G, J
  C: F, G, J
  B: J, L
  D: F, G, J, L
Response 0:
Thought:
  M and N are separated by lunch which means they cannot speak consecutively.
  There is only one speaker between M and N.
  From (4), it can be concluded that the speaker between M and N must be either J or L.
  From (2), we know that there are three speakers before lunch and three speakers after lunch.
  From (3), we know that G must speak before lunch.
  From (5), F speaks in the first or third place.
  Considering all the above, the speakers arranged between M and N can only be J and L.
  Therefore, the answer is B: J, L.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  G must speak before lunch and three speakers speak before lunch, including G.
  Therefore, two of the speakers G, J, and L will speak before lunch. So, M and N should speak after lunch.
  F speaks in the first or third place, which means M and N can't speak in the third place.
  If M speaks before lunch, then N will speak after lunch, and only L will be between M and N.
  If N speaks before lunch, then M will speak after lunch, and only J will be between M and N.
  Therefore, the list of all speakers that can be arranged between M and N is either J, L or L, J.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  M and N are separated by lunch.
  So, we have two groups of three speakers: (G, J, and one other speaker before lunch) and (L, F, and one other speaker after lunch).
  From 4th condition, we know that only one speaker is between M and N.
  Therefore, either M or N should be in the group before lunch along with G and J.
  From 5th condition, we know that F speaks in the first or third place.
  If F speaks first, L and N must speak after lunch, and G, J, M must speak before lunch. Thus, J is the only speaker that can be arranged between M and N.
  If F speaks third, J and G must speak before lunch, and L, M, and N must speak after lunch. Thus, J, L, and F are the only speakers that can be arranged between M and N.
  Therefore, list of all speakers that can be arranged between M and N is either J only (A), or J, L, and F (C).

- Based on the above conditions, we could use paper H or not, depending on whether we use paper G or not.

No paper J, but paper K.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 22 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: In a cooking competition, the chef is required to make one hot dish and one cold dish, and the results are evaluated as "top grade", "middle grade", and "bottom grade".If each result of the chef is not lower than that of Chef B, and at least one item is higher than Chef B, it is said that "Chef A is more skilled than Chef B".There are a number of existing chefs, none of them is more skilled than the other, and no two people have the same hot dishes and cold dishes.
Question: How many chefs can meet the above conditions?
Choices:
  A: unconfirmed
  B: 9 people
  C: 6 people
  D: 3 people
Response 0:
Thought:
  According to the given context, for two chefs to be compared in terms of skill, if each result of Chef A is not lower than that of Chef B, and at least one item is higher than Chef B, then Chef A is more skilled than Chef B.
  Also, it is said that none of the chefs are more skilled than others.
  Therefore, if there are 3 chefs A, B, and C, then if A is more skilled than B and B is more skilled than C, then A is also more skilled than Chef C, which contradicts the given condition.
  Therefore, at least 4 chefs are needed where no two people have the same hot dishes and cold dishes.
  There are 3 possible grades (top, middle, bottom).
  Therefore, there are a total of 3x3 = 9 possible combinations of grades for each person.
  Since no two people have the same dishes, the first person has 9 choices, the second person has 8 choices, and the third person has 7 choices.
  So, the number of ways to choose 3 people out of 9 is C(9,3) = 84.
  Thus, there can be 84 chefs who meet the given conditions.
  The answer is therefore unconfirmed.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  There are no two people with the same hot dishes and cold dishes.
  Therefore, there are (the number of hot dishes) * (the number of cold dishes) different combinations of dishes for each person.
  There are three levels of results: top, middle, and bottom.
  If each result of chef A is not lower than that of Chef B, and at least one item is higher than Chef B, then Chef A is more skilled than Chef B.
  Since there are no chefs with the same dishes, each chef's skill level can only be compared to other chefs on the basis of someone's dishes being better than the other.
  Therefore, each chef's skill level must be unique.
  Since there are three levels of results and all chefs are equally skilled, there can be no more than three chefs.
  Let's suppose there are three chefs, A, B, and C.
  Without loss of generality, assume that Chef A's hot dish is better than B's, and Chef B's cold dish is better than C's.
  Then Chef A's skill level is higher than that of B, and Chef B's skill level is higher than that of C. 
  Therefore, Chef A's skill level must be higher than that of C, which contradicts the assumption that there is no more skilled chef. 
  Therefore, it is impossible for there to be more than two chefs.
  We have shown that there are no more than two chefs, and there must be at least two chefs with distinct dishes.
  Since there are three dishes for each course, there are 3*3=9 distinct dishes in total.
  Therefore, there are 9 different ways to assign one hot dish and one cold dish to each of the two chefs.
  So there are 9 possible combinations of two chefs.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 6 people.

When the economy in a region is sluggish, many people are unemployed, so they reduce their living expenses, resulting in more unemployment and worsening the economy.The economy continued to deteriorate, and finally prices fell to the lowest point.Low prices have stimulated people to increase their living consumption, and increased consumption has led to improved economic conditions.Li Ming? Choices:
  A: The greatest philosophers in the world prefer to avoid intimate relationships.
  B: People with intimate relationships rarely spend their time alone.
  C: Loneliness is necessary for philosophers to meditate.
  D: The greatest philosophers in the world are happy.

The assumptions made are:
- The happiness of the greatest philosophers is relevant to the psychological theory.
- The greatest philosophers were not happy.
- The intimate relationships of the greatest philosophers were studied.

Topic: Logic
Context: A unit arranges for 6 people on duty on the first day, second day, third day of the new year.They are G., H, K, L, P, and S.Two people are required per day.The personnel arrangement must meet the following conditions? (1) L and P must be on duty on the same day.(2) G and H cannot be on duty on the same day.(3) If K is on the first day of duty, then G is on the second day of duty.(4 ) If S is on the third day of duty, then H is on the second day of duty.
Question: If H is on duty the same day before S, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: G on the second day of duty
  B: P on duty in the second day
  C: K on duty in the first day
  D: H on duty at the first day
Response 0:
Thought: 
  H is on duty the same day before S.
  If S is on the third day of duty, then H is on the second day of duty.
  Therefore, S is on the third day and H is on the second day.

  Therefore, H cannot be on the first day, and G should be on the first day.
  If K is on the first day of duty, then G is on the second day of duty.
  Therefore, K cannot be on the first day, and G should be on the second day.
  L and P must be on duty on the same day.
  Therefore, L and P should be on the first day.
  Hence, K is on the third day.
  Therefore, P cannot be on the second day, and K should be on the first day.
  The only option that must be true is A: G on the second day of duty.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 38 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: It is no longer new for college students to take vacation as a nanny.A survey showed that 63% of the respondents favored college students as nanny, but when asked if they would ask college students to be nanny, nearly 60% said "no".
Question: Which of the following statements, if true, can reasonably explain the seemingly contradictory phenomenon?
Choices:
  A: Among those who choose to "will invite college students to be nanny", 75% intend to let college students work as tutors or secretaries, and only 25% want college students to do housework.
  B: 62% of the people in the survey indicated that they were only willing to pay a monthly salary of 800 yuan to 1,000 yuan for the college nanny.
  C: Among those who favor college students as nanny, 69% think that doing housekeeping work is good for college students themselves, and only 31% think that college students nanny can provide better housekeeping services.
  D: Among those who do not approve of college students being nanny, 40% believe that students should choose a field related to their major in practice.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The survey showed that 63% of the respondents favored college students as nanny, but when asked if they would ask college students to be nanny, nearly 60% said "no".
  Statement A talks about how those who choose to "will invite college students to be nanny" intend to let college students work as tutors or secretaries instead of housework. Statement A only explains the apparent contradiction if we assume that the 60% of respondents who said they would not ask college students to be nanny did so because they do not want college students to do housework. But this assumption is not given in the question stem.
  Statement B talks about the amount of salary respondents are willing to pay the college nanny, but it does not explain the contradiction. 
  Statement C says that among those who favor college students as nanny, the majority thinks that doing housekeeping work is good for college students themselves, and not necessarily because they provide better housekeeping services.   B: First on Q

(1) Dr.Zhang is only responsible for treating male patients.(2) Dr.Li can only be responsible for the treatment of 1 patient.(3) If a doctor is responsible for treating a child patient, then he must be responsible for the treatment of an adult patient of the same sex as the child.
Question: According to the question, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: Dr.Wang is responsible for treating at least one female patient.
  B: Dr.Wang is responsible for treating at least one child patient.
  C: Dr.Liu is responsible for treating at least one male patient.
  D: Dr.Liu is responsible for treating at least one child patient.

  A) We do not know if Dr.Wang is responsible for treating any females, so this statement cannot be true.
  B) There are only two child patients, J and K, and we do not know if Dr.Wang is responsible for either of them, so this statement cannot be true.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are 7 candidates hired by Haier? F, G, H, I, W, X and Y.One of them needs to be assigned to the public relations department, three to the production department, and the other three to the sales department.The personnel allocation of these 7 employees must meet the following conditions? (1) H and Y must be allocated in the same department.(2) F and G cannot be allocated in the same department (3) If X is allocated in the sales department, W is allocated in the production department.(4) F must be allocated in the production department.
Question: Which of the following may list the final distribution of these 7 employees?
Choices:
  A: Public Relations Department? W; Production Department? F, H, Y; Sales Department? G, I, X
  B: Public Relations Department? W; Production Department? G, I, X; Sales Department? F, H, Y
  C: Public Relations Department? X; Production Department? F, G, H; Sales Department? I, Y, W
  D: Public Relations Department? X; Production Department? F, I, W; Sales Department? G, H, Y
Response 0:
Thought:
  F must be allocated in the Production Department.
  H and Y must be allocated in the same department.
  If X is in the Sales Department, W is allocated in the Production Department.
  F cannot be with G.
  Only one person can be assigned to the Public Relations Department.
  
  From F, we can know that 1 person is already assigned in the Production Department.
  H and Y should be assigned in the same department
  If W is not in production, X cannot be in sales, leading to G, I, and Y in sales
  Therefore, W is in Production and X is in Sales, then H and Y are also in Sales.
  And, F cannot be in sales. Therefore, F and G are in Production and I is in the Public Relations Department.
  The final distribution should be: Public Relations Department? I; Production Department? F, G, W; Sales Department? H, X, Y
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  According to the conditions given, H and Y must be allocated in the same department, so we have limited options to allocate them in Production or Sales department.
  F and G cannot be allocated in the same department; so F must be allocated in Production, and in that case, G cannot be allocated in Production.
  If X is allocated in Sales, we must allocate W in Production. Therefore, we can allocate I and Y to Sales department, and H to Production.
  So, based on the above conditions, the final distribution of these 7 employees could be - Public Relations Department: X, Production Department: F, H, W and Sales Department: G, I, Y.
  So, the answer is D: Public Relations Department? X; Production Department? F, I, W; Sales Department? G, H, Y.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We need to follow four conditions while distributing these 7 employees to different departments.
  (1) H and Y must be allocated in the same department: H and Y can be allocated to either production or sales department.
  (2) F and G cannot be allocated in the same department: F and G can be allocated to public relations, production or sales department, but both cannot be together in any department.
  (3) If X is allocated in the sales department, W is allocated in the production department: This condition ensures that we cannot allocate X and W to different departments.

  A: Are all the interviewees saying in the survey true?

Context: The members of the printing group and the binding group are mainly from the following seven employees-F, G, H, J, K, L and M.The members of each group must meet the following conditions? (1) Each group has at least 3 employees .(2) F and K cannot be in the same group.(3) If K is in a certain group, J must also be in this group.(4) M is at least one of the members of these two groups.(5) At least one of the same employees in both groups.
Question: If both K and L are members of both groups, and the printing group has exactly three members, which of the following statements must be true?
Choices:
  A: F in printing group
  B: F in the binding group
  C: G in the printing group
  D: M in the bookbinding group
Response 0:
Thought:
  K and L are members of both groups.
  The printing group has exactly three members.
  If K is in a certain group, J must also be in this group.
  Let's try to list all conditions and constraints:
    - If K is in a certain group, J must also be in this group.
    - F and K cannot be in the same group.
    - M is at least one of the members of these two groups.
    - At least one of the same employees in both groups.
    - Each group has at least 3 employees.
    - The printing group has exactly three members.
  We know that K and L are members of both groups. This means that the printing group has exactly two other members other than K and L. 
  We have to consider the possibilities:
    - K in the printing group and L in the binding group
      If K in the printing group, J must also be in the printing group. Therefore, we have K, L, and J in the printing group. This means F, G, and H are in the binding group. M can be in either group.
      Since we are looking for a must-be-true statement, we can eliminate choices C and D since they are not necessarily true for all possibilities.
      Both F and K are in the binding group, so F in the binding group is must be true. 
      Therefore, the answer is B.
    - K in the binding group and L in the printing group
      If K is in the binding group, J must also be in the binding group. Therefore, we have K, L, and J in the binding group. This means F, G, and H are in the printing group. M can be in either group.
      Since we are looking for a must-be-true statement, we can eliminate choices C and D since they are not necessarily true for all possibilities.
      Both F and K are in the printing group, so F in the printing group can be true. However, it is not necessarily true for all possibilities.
      Therefore, the answer is B.

(1) If G or H is arranged to play, they must be in the front.Bit.(2) If K is scheduled to play, he must be in the middle.(3) If L is scheduled to play, he must be on team 1.(4) Neither P nor K can be in the same team as N.(5) P cannot be in the same team as Q.(6) If H is in team 2, Q is in the middle of team 1.
Question: If H is in Team 2, which of the listed arrangements is acceptable for Team 1?
Choices:

Question: Which of the following is most helpful in eliminating this inconsistency?
Choices:
  A: Severe investigations of drunk driving have occurred in urban traffic accidents.
  B: The city that implements strict investigation of drunk driving has not eliminated drunk driving.
  C: It is more important to improve drivers' traffic safety awareness than strict management.
  D: In addition to strict investigation of drunk driving, other traffic violations should also be stopped.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The survey reports that the incidence of traffic accidents is similar despite strict investigation of drunk driving suggests that something else is causing the accidents.
  The common belief among experts is that strict investigation can reduce the occurrence of traffic accidents.
  The inconsistency is how the survey results and the experts' belief differ.
  To eliminate the inconsistency, we need to find something that reconciles the difference between the survey results and the experts' belief.
  Option A does not provide any additional information relevant to the inconsistency. 
  Option B suggests that drunk driving still exists in cities with strict investigation, which means that strict investigation alone may not solve the problem. It reconciles the difference between the survey results and the experts' belief. 
  Option C and D present reasonable and useful suggestions, but they do not help reconcile the inconsistency presented.
  Therefore, the answer is B: The city that implements strict investigation of drunk driving has not eliminated drunk driving.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are 6 warehouses in a warehouse, in order from 1 to 6.There are 6 kinds of goods F, G, L, M, P, T.Each warehouse stores exactly one of 6 kinds of goods, and different kinds of goods cannot be stored in the same warehouse.The following conditions must also be met when storing goods? (1) The warehouse number for storing G is larger than the warehouse number for storing L.(2) The warehouse number storing L is larger than the warehouse number storing T.(3) The warehouse number storing P is larger than the warehouse number storing F.(4) The warehouse storing T is next to the warehouse storing P.
Question: If there is exactly one warehouse between the warehouse where M is stored and the warehouse where G is stored, how many kinds of goods are stored in the warehouse?
Choices:
  A: 2 rooms
  B: 3 rooms
  C: 4
  D: 5 rooms
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's mark the six warehouses as W1, W2, W3, W4, W5, W6 from left to right.
  Let's mark the six kinds of goods as F, G, L, M, P, T respectively.
  From Condition (1), we know that G > L.
  From Condition (2), we know that L > T.
  From Condition (3), we know that P > F.
  From Condition (4), we know that |T - P| = 1.
  Let's assume that the warehouse where M is stored is Wx, then the warehouse where G is stored should be either Wx + 2 or Wx - 2.
  However, since there are only six warehouses, neither Wx + 2 nor Wx - 2 can be greater than W6 or less than W1.
  Therefore, there are only two possibilities for the warehouse where M is stored: W1, W2.
  If the warehouse where M is stored is W1, then the warehouse where G is stored is W3.
  Then we can know that F must be in the warehouse W1 according to Condition (3), and T must be in the warehouse W4 according to Condition (4).
  Then, L must be in warehouse W5 following Condition (2).
  Therefore, there are two kinds of goods stored in the warehouse: G and P.
  If the warehouse where M is stored is W2, then the warehouse where G is stored is W4.
  Then according to Condition (1), L must be in the warehouse W3.
  According to Condition (3), F must be in the warehouse W1. According to Condition (4), T must be in the warehouse W5.
  Therefore, there are two kinds of goods stored in the warehouse: L and P.
  Combining the two possibilities, there are two kinds of goods stored in the warehouse: G and P or L and P.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  If there is exactly one warehouse between the warehouse where M is stored and the warehouse where G is stored, we can infer that G and M are not stored in adjacent warehouses.
  Condition (1) tells us that the the warehouse number storing G is larger than the warehouse number storing L, but does not tell us the exact positions of G and L.
  Condition (2) tells us that the warehouse storing L is larger than the warehouse storing T, but does not tell us the exact positions of L and T.
  Condition (3) tells us that the warehouse number storing P is larger than the warehouse number storing F, but does not tell us the exact positions of P and F.
  Condition (4) tells us that the warehouse storing T is next to the warehouse storing P.
  Let's try to work backwards and deduce how many kinds of goods are stored in the warehouse:
  If T is stored in warehouse 4 and P is stored in warehouse 5, then M must be stored in warehouse 2 and G would have to be stored in either warehouse 1 or 6, but neither of these scenarios would satisfy the condition that there is exactly one warehouse between the warehouse where M is stored and the warehouse where G is stored. Hence, we can rule out this scenario. 
  If T is stored in warehouse 5 and P is stored in warehouse 6, then G must be stored in warehouse 1 and L must be stored in warehouse 2. Then, M and F would have to be stored in warehouses 3 and 4 in some order. In this case, there are 4 kinds of goods stored in the warehouse. Hence, we have found one valid scenario that satisfies the given conditions. 
  Therefore, the answer is C: 4.

  - M and G can only be in warehouses 3 and 4, in any order.

  - T and P must then be in warehouses 1 and 2.
  - F then can only be in warehouse 5 or 6.
  Therefore, in all possible cases, there are 4 kinds of goods stored in the warehouse.
  The answer is C: 4.

Topic: Logic
Context: A company has six general manager assistants F, G, H, I, M and P, and three departments, each of which is in charge of three general manager assistants.Each assistant general manager is in charge of at least one department.The following conditions must be met? (1) There is only one assistant to the general manager in charge of three departments at the same time.(2) F and G are not in charge of the same department.(3) H and I are not in charge of the same department.
Question: If F and M are not in charge of the same department, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: F and H are in charge of the same department.
  B: F and I are in charge of the same department.
  C: I and P are in charge of the same department.
  D: M and G are in charge of the same department.
Response 0:
Thought:
  There are three departments, each managed by three assistant general managers.
  There is only one assistant general manager in charge of three departments.
  Let's assume F and M are not in charge of the same department.
  This means that F and M are both in charge of two departments. 
  If F is not in the same department as M, then F must be in different departments with the assistant general managers already assigned to the two departments with which M is in charge of.
  Given that H and I cannot be in the same department, then it means that either F or M is in charge of a department with H or I.
  Therefore, either F or M is in charge of a department with I.
  Therefore, F and I are in charge of the same department.
  The answer is B: F and I are in charge of the same department.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If F and M are not in charge of the same department, we must consider possible combinations of departments they can be in charge of.
  If either F or M is in a department with three assistants and the other is in a different department, there would be a violation of condition (1).
  Therefore, both F and M have to be in departments with two assistants.
  The only other assistant available to be in a department with F is H; the only other assistant available to be in a department with M is G. 
  Therefore, H and G cannot be in the same department, as that would mean two assistants are in charge of three departments, violating condition (1).
  From (2), we know that F and G cannot be in the same department.
  From (3), we know that H and I cannot be in the same department.
  Therefore, F and I cannot be in the same department, eliminating choice (B).
  This leaves only choice (A) as a possibility, but we need to confirm this doesn't violate any of the conditions. We see that F and H can be in the same department, M and P must be in the same department because they're the only two left, and this leaves I and G to be in the same department, which doesn't violate any of the three conditions.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: A music producer is recording 7 albums one after another? F, G, H, J, K, L and M, but it is not necessary to record in this order.When arranging the sequence of recording these 7 albums, the following conditions must be met? (l) F must be ranked second.(2) J cannot be ranked seventh.(3) G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H.(4) H must be somewhere in front of L.(5) L must be somewhere before M.
Question: If M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: K seventh
  B: L third
  C: H is either in front of F or immediately after F
  D: L either immediately before G or immediately after G
Response 0:
Thought:
  The sequence for the albums must follow the following conditions:
  1. F must be ranked second.
  2. J cannot be ranked seventh.
  3. G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H.
  4. H must be somewhere in front of L.
  5. L must be somewhere before M.
  If M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K, then L must be before K. Therefore, K cannot be seventh. 
  There is no evidence supporting that L must be third. L is before M and K. Therefore, L cannot be ranked third. 
  G cannot be immediately after H. Therefore, G must be immediately before H. H is in front of L. Therefore, H cannot be immediately after G. So, H is either in front of F or immediately after F. 
  L is before K. Therefore, L cannot be immediately before G or immediately after G. 
  Therefore, the answer is C: H is either in front of F or immediately after F.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K
  There are many possible sequences but we can narrow down our search using the given conditions.
  F must be ranked second and L must be somewhere before M
  G cannot be directly in front of H nor immediately after H and H must be somewhere in front of L.
  J cannot be ranked seventh.
  From condition 1 we know that F is second, then from condition 3, G cannot be third thus G is fourth. From condition 5 if L is before M then L cannot be third.
  Since J cannot be ranked seventh then H must be seventh. So we have the sequence _ F G _ _ _ L H M or _ F G _ _ _ H L M. Since H is before L, L cannot be seventh. Therefore we have the sequence _ F G _ _ _ L H M.
  Thus we can conclude that L is before H.
  Therefore, the answer is D: L either immediately before G or immediately after G. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  If M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K,
  there are three possible positions for M:
    (1) M is first, then J and K must be in positions two and three.
    (2) M is second, then F is first and J and K must be in positions three and four.
    (3) M is third, then F is first and J and K must be in positions four and five.
  Based on (l), F must be ranked second.
  Therefore, the possible position of M is the third one, which implies J and K are in the fourth and fifth positions.
  Based on (4), H must be somewhere in front of L; therefore H is either in position 1 or 2.
  Based on (5), L must be somewhere before M; therefore L is in position 3.
  Based on (2), J cannot be ranked seventh; therefore, J is in position 4.
  Based on (3), G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H; therefore, G is in position 7, 6 or 4.
  Based on (5), L must be somewhere before M; therefore, G cannot be immediately after L. 
  Therefore, the only possible arrangement for G, H, and L is G in position 4, L in position 3, and H in position 1.
  Thus, the only possible position for F is position 2. 
  Therefore, C is true, which is "H is either in front of F or immediately after F."
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought:
  M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K.
  This means that M can be either before J or in between J and K.
  Conditions (1, 2, 3, 4, and 5) must be met.
  Condition (5) states that L must be somewhere before M.
  Therefore, M must be ranked sixth or seventh.
  If M is ranked seventh, then J must be ranked sixth (due to condition 2).
  If M is ranked sixth, then J must be ranked seventh.
  If J is ranked seventh, then H must be ranked sixth (due to condition 4).
  If J is ranked sixth, then the position of H is not determined yet.
  Condition (3) states that G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H. If H is ranked fifth, then G can only be ranked third or fourth (due to condition 3).
  If H is ranked fourth, then L must be ranked third (due to condition 5).
  If H is ranked fifth, then L must be ranked third or fourth.

Topic: Logic
Context: Crimes involving the use of firearms are more likely to lead to murder than other types of crimes.However, most crimes involving the use of firearms did not result in homicides.Therefore, there is no need to distinguish the illegal use of firearms as a serious criminal offense in the criminal law from other criminal offenses.
Question: The logic loophole in the above argument is most similar to the following one?
Choices:
  A: Obese people are more likely to suffer from heart disease than people with normal weight.However, obese people make up a very small percentage of our population.Therefore, in our country, there is no need for the medical and health community to emphasize the risk of heart disease.
  B: Unchecked sex is more likely to be infected with AIDS than checkpoint.However, among people with unchecked sex, only a small percentage of people are infected with AIDS.Therefore, there is no need to emphasize the harm of unchecked sex in the propaganda of AIDS prevention.
  C: The prevailing view is that smoking is more likely to cause lung cancer than not smoking.However, in some countries, the proportion of people with lung cancer who have a history of smoking is not higher than the proportion of the total population who have a history of smoking.Therefore, the above popular opinion is likely to be a prejudice.
  D: High-income people are more capable of enjoying life than low-income people.But there are many high-income earners who claim to be unhappy.Therefore, those who pursue a happy life need not pay attention to the level of income.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The argument suggests that since most crimes involving firearms do not result in homicides, there's no need to distinguish illegal use of firearms as a serious criminal offense. 
  The argument is flawed since it ignores the possibility that illegal use of firearms could result in serious, non-fatal injuries or other crimes such as armed robbery.
  Choice B has a similar logic loophole that ignores the possibility of other harms associated with unchecked sex.
 Action: Answer("B")
